Communications Ltd)</li></ul></div></li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Guernsey</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\xa1/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">\xc9\xa1</span><span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Guernsey.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bd/En-Guernsey.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Guernsey.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>) is an island in the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>. It lies roughly north of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Malo" title="Saint-Malo">Saint-Malo</a> and to the west of <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cotentin_Peninsula" title="Cotentin Peninsula">Cotentin Peninsula</a>. With several smaller nearby islands, it forms a jurisdiction within the <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Guernsey" title="Bailiwick of Guernsey">Bailiwick of Guernsey</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependency</a>. The jurisdiction is made up of <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Guernsey" title="Parishes of Guernsey">ten parishes</a> on the island of Guernsey, three other inhabited islands (<a href="/wiki/Herm" title="Herm">Herm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jethou" title="Jethou">Jethou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lihou" title="Lihou">Lihou</a>), and many small islets and rocks.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Society"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Society</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_status">Constitutional status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Constitutional status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The jurisdiction is not part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, although defence and most foreign relations are handled by the British Government.<sup id="cite_ref-Ogier_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ogier-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The entire jurisdiction lies within the <a href="/wiki/Common_Travel_Area" title="Common Travel Area">Common Travel Area</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> and is not a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, but has a special relationship with it, being treated as part of the European Community with access to the single market for the purposes of free trade in goods. Taken together with the separate jurisdictions of <a href="/wiki/Alderney" title="Alderney">Alderney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sark" title="Sark">Sark</a> it forms the Bailiwick of Guernsey.\n</p><p>The two Bailiwicks of Guernsey and <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> together form the geographical grouping known as the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name "Guernsey", as well as that of neighbouring "<a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>", is of <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> origin. The second element of each word, "<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-ey" class="extiw" title="wikt:-ey">-ey</a>", is the Old Norse for "island",<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> while the original root, "guern(s)", is of uncertain origin and meaning, possibly deriving from either a personal name such as Grani or Warinn, or from <i>gron</i>, meaning pine tree.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Previous names for the Channel Islands vary over history, but include the <i>Lenur</i> islands,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Sarnia</i>, Sarnia is the Latin name for Guernsey, or <i>Lisia</i> (Guernsey) and <i>Angia</i> (Jersey).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guernsey" title="History of Guernsey">History of Guernsey</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Maritime_history_of_the_Channel_Islands" title="Maritime history of the Channel Islands">Maritime history of the Channel Islands</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Around 6000&#160;BC, rising seas created the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> and separated the <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Norman</a> <a href="/wiki/Promontory" title="Promontory">promontories</a> that became the bailiwicks of Guernsey and Jersey from <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> farmers then settled on its coast and built the <a href="/wiki/Dolmen" title="Dolmen">dolmens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Menhir" title="Menhir">menhirs</a> found in the islands today, providing evidence of human presence dating back to around 5000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Evidence of Roman settlements on the island, and the discovery of <a href="/wiki/Amphora" title="Amphora">amphorae</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Herculaneum" title="Herculaneum">Herculaneum</a> area and Spain, show evidence of an intricate trading network with regional and long distance trade.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Buildings found in La Plaiderie, St Peter Port dating from 100\xe2\x80\x93400 AD appear to be warehouses.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The earliest evidence of shipping was the discovery of a wreck in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_Port_Harbour" title="Saint Peter Port Harbour">St Peter Port harbor</a> of a ship, which has been named "Asterix". It is thought to be a 3rd-century Roman cargo vessel and was probably at anchor or grounded when the fire broke out.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Travelling from the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Gwent" title="Kingdom of Gwent">Kingdom of Gwent</a>, Saint <a href="/wiki/Samson_of_Dol" title="Samson of Dol">Sampson</a>, later the abbot of <a href="/wiki/Dol-de-Bretagne" title="Dol-de-Bretagne">Dol</a> in Brittany, is credited with the introduction of Christianity to Guernsey.<sup id="cite_ref-HoG_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoG-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 933, the <a href="/wiki/Cotentin_Peninsula" title="Cotentin Peninsula">Cotentin Peninsula</a> including <a href="/wiki/Avranchin" title="Avranchin">Avranchin</a> which included the islands, were placed by the French <a href="/wiki/Rudolph_of_France" title="Rudolph of France">King Ranulf</a> under the control of <a href="/wiki/William_I_Longsword" class="mw-redirect" title="William I Longsword">William I</a>. The island of Guernsey and the other <a href="/wiki/Channel_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Channel Island">Channel Islands</a> represent the last remnants of the medieval <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Normandy" title="Duchy of Normandy">Duchy of Normandy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HoG_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoG-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 1204, when <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">King John</a> lost the continental portion of the Duchy to <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_France" title="Philip II of France">Philip II of France</a>, the islands remained part of the kingdom of England.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The islands were then recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1259)" title="Treaty of Paris (1259)">1259 Treaty of Paris</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">Henry III</a>\'s territories.<sup id="cite_ref-Ogier_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ogier-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the island was a haven for pirates that would use the "lamping technique" to ground ships close to her waters. This intensified during the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred Years War">Hundred Years War</a>, when, <a href="/wiki/English_Channel_naval_campaign,_1338-1339" class="mw-redirect" title="English Channel naval campaign, 1338-1339">starting in 1339</a>, the island was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_dynasty" title="Capetian dynasty">Capetians</a> on several occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-HoG_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoG-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Guernsey_Militia" title="Royal Guernsey Militia">Guernsey Militia</a> was first mentioned as operational in 1331 and would help defend the island for a further 600 years.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1372, the island was invaded by <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragonese</a> mercenaries under the command of <a href="/wiki/Owain_Lawgoch" title="Owain Lawgoch">Owain Lawgoch</a> (remembered as <i>Yvon de Galles</i>), who was in the pay of the French king. Owain and his dark-haired mercenaries were later absorbed into Guernsey legend as invading <a href="/wiki/Fairy" title="Fairy">fairies</a> from across the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As part of the peace between England and France, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Sixtus_IV" title="Pope Sixtus IV">Pope Sixtus IV</a> issued in 1483 a <a href="/wiki/Papal_bull" title="Papal bull">Papal bull</a> granting the <i>Privilege of Neutrality</i>, by which the Islands, their harbours and seas, as far as the eye can see, were considered neutral territory.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Anyone molesting Islanders would be excommunicated. A <a href="/wiki/Royal_charters_applying_to_the_Channel_Islands" title="Royal charters applying to the Channel Islands">Royal Charter</a> in 1548 confirmed the neutrality. The French attempted to invade Jersey a year later in 1549 but were defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Militia_of_the_Island_of_Jersey" title="Royal Militia of the Island of Jersey">militia</a>. The neutrality lasted another century, until <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William III of England</a> abolished the privilege due to privateering activity against Dutch ships.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the mid-16th century, the island was influenced by <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinist</a> reformers from Normandy. During the <a href="/wiki/Marian_persecutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Marian persecutions">Marian persecutions</a>, three women, the <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Martyrs" title="Guernsey Martyrs">Guernsey Martyrs</a>, were <a href="/wiki/Burned_at_the_stake" class="mw-redirect" title="Burned at the stake">burned at the stake</a> for their <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Cornet_Floodlit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Castle_Cornet_Floodlit.jpg/300px-Castle_Cornet_Floodlit.jpg" width="300" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Castle_Cornet_Floodlit.jpg/450px-Castle_Cornet_Floodlit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Castle_Cornet_Floodlit.jpg/600px-Castle_Cornet_Floodlit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1295" data-file-height="567" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Cornet_Floodlit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Castle_Cornet" title="Castle Cornet">Castle Cornet</a> seen at night over the harbour of <a href="/wiki/St_Peter_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="St Peter Port">St Peter Port</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, Guernsey sided with the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarians</a>. The allegiance was not total, however; there were a few Royalist uprisings in the southwest of the island, while <a href="/wiki/Castle_Cornet" title="Castle Cornet">Castle Cornet</a> was occupied by the Governor, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Osborne_(1584-1653)" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter Osborne (1584-1653)">Sir Peter Osborne</a>, and Royalist troops. In December 1651, with full honours of war, Castle Cornet surrendered \xe2\x80\x93 the last Royalist outpost anywhere in the British Isles to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Wars against France and Spain during the 17th and 18th centuries gave Guernsey shipowners and sea captains the opportunity to exploit the island\'s proximity to mainland Europe by applying for <a href="/wiki/Letter_of_marque" title="Letter of marque">letters of marque</a> and turning their <a href="/wiki/Cargo_ship" title="Cargo ship">merchantmen</a> into <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a>.\n</p><p>By the beginning of the 18th century, Guernsey\'s residents were starting to settle in North America,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> in particular founding <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_County,_Ohio" title="Guernsey County, Ohio">Guernsey County</a> in Ohio in 1810.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The threat of invasion by <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> prompted many defensive structures to be built at the end of that century.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The early 19th century saw a dramatic increase in the prosperity of the island, due to its success in the global <a href="/wiki/Maritime_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime trade">maritime trade</a>, and the rise of the stone industry. Maritime trade suffered a major decline with the move away from sailing craft as materials such as iron and steel were not available on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Braye_du_Valle,_Guernsey" title="Braye du Valle, Guernsey">Le Braye du Valle</a> was a tidal channel that made the northern extremity of Guernsey, Le Clos du Valle, a <a href="/wiki/Tidal_island" title="Tidal island">tidal island</a>. Le Braye du Valle was drained and reclaimed in 1806 by the British Government as a defence measure. The eastern end of the former channel became the town and harbour (from 1820) of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Sampson,_Guernsey" title="Saint Sampson, Guernsey">St Sampson\'s</a>, now the second biggest port in Guernsey. The western end of La Braye is now Le Grand Havre. The roadway called "The Bridge" across the end of the harbour at St Sampson\'s recalls the bridge that formerly linked the two parts of Guernsey at high tide. New roads were built and main roads metalled for ease of use by the military.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_period">Contemporary period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Contemporary period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_island.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Guernsey_island.jpg/300px-Guernsey_island.jpg" width="300" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Guernsey_island.jpg/450px-Guernsey_island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Guernsey_island.jpg/600px-Guernsey_island.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1326" data-file-height="715" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_island.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The island of Guernsey seen from 33,000 feet (10,000&#160;m), looking north</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, about 3,000 island men served in the <a href="/wiki/British_Expeditionary_Force_(World_War_I)" title="British Expeditionary Force (World War I)">British Expeditionary Force</a>. Of these, about 1,000 served in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Guernsey_Light_Infantry" title="Royal Guernsey Light Infantry">Royal Guernsey Light Infantry</a> regiment formed from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Guernsey_Militia" title="Royal Guernsey Militia">Royal Guernsey Militia</a> in 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 30 June 1940, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>,  the Channel Islands were <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_the_Channel_Islands" title="German occupation of the Channel Islands">occupied by German troops</a>. Before the occupation, 80% of <a href="/wiki/Evacuation_of_civilians_from_the_Channel_Islands_in_1940" title="Evacuation of civilians from the Channel Islands in 1940">Guernsey children had been evacuated</a> to England to live with relatives or strangers during the war. Some children were never reunited with their families.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The occupying German forces <a href="/wiki/Deportations_from_the_German-occupied_Channel_Islands" title="Deportations from the German-occupied Channel Islands">deported over 1,000 Guernsey residents</a> to camps in southern Germany, notably to the <i>Lager Lindele</i> (Lindele Camp) near <a href="/wiki/Biberach_an_der_Ri%C3%9F" class="mw-redirect" title="Biberach an der Ri\xc3\x9f">Biberach an der Ri\xc3\x9f</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Laufen,_Germany" title="Laufen, Germany">Laufen</a>. <a href="/wiki/German_fortification_of_Guernsey" title="German fortification of Guernsey">Guernsey was very heavily fortified during World War II</a>, out of all proportion to the island\'s strategic value. German defences and alterations remain visible, particularly to Castle Cornet and around the northern coast of the island. The island was liberated on 9 May 1945, now celebrated as <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day_(Channel_Islands)" title="Liberation Day (Channel Islands)">Liberation Day</a> across both Guernsey and Jersey.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the late 1940s the island repaired the damage caused to its buildings during the occupation. The tomato industry started up again and thrived until the 1970s when it hit a sharp, terminal decline.<sup id="cite_ref-Tomato_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tomato-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Tourism has remained important.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Finance businesses grew in the 1970s and expanded in the next two decades and are important employers.<sup id="cite_ref-Crossan17_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crossan17-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Guernsey\'s constitutional and trading relationships with the United Kingdom and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> will be unaffected by <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_sm02.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Guernsey_sm02.png/220px-Guernsey_sm02.png" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/Guernsey_sm02.png 1.5x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="350" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_sm02.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Guernsey and its sister islands that make up the Bailiwick</div></div></div>\n<p>Situated around <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Guernsey&amp;params=49_35_N_2_20_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">49\xc2\xb035\xe2\x80\xb2N</span> <span class="longitude">2\xc2\xb020\xe2\x80\xb2W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">49.583\xc2\xb0N 2.333\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">49.583; -2.333</span></span></span></a></span>, Guernsey, Herm and some other smaller islands together have a total area of 71 square kilometres (27&#160;sq&#160;mi) and coastlines of about 46 kilometres (29&#160;mi). Elevation varies from sea level to 110&#160;m (360&#160;ft) at Hautnez on Guernsey.\n</p><p>There are many smaller <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_Bailiwick_of_Guernsey" title="List of islands of the Bailiwick of Guernsey">islands, islets, rocks and reefs</a> in Guernsey waters. Combined with a tidal range of 10 metres (33 feet) and fast currents of up to 12 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">knots</a>, this makes sailing in local waters dangerous. The very large tidal variation provides an environmentally rich inter-tidal zone around the islands, and some sites have received <a href="/wiki/Ramsar_Convention" title="Ramsar Convention">Ramsar Convention</a> designation.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Guernsey\'s climate is temperate with mild winters and warm, sunny summers. It is classified as an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, with a dry-summer trend, although marginally wetter than <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">mediterranean</a> summers. The warmest months are July and August, when temperatures are generally around 20&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68&#160;\xc2\xb0F) with some days occasionally going above 24&#160;\xc2\xb0C (75&#160;\xc2\xb0F). On average, the coldest month is February with an average weekly mean air temperature of 6&#160;\xc2\xb0C (42.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Average weekly mean air temperature reaches 16&#160;\xc2\xb0C (60.8&#160;\xc2\xb0F) in August. Snow rarely falls and is unlikely to settle, but is most likely to fall in February. The temperature rarely drops below freezing, although strong wind-chill from Arctic winds can sometimes make it feel like it. The rainiest months are December (average 112&#160;mm (4.4&#160;in)), November (average 104&#160;mm (4.09&#160;in)) and January (average 92&#160;mm (3.62&#160;in)). July is, on average, the sunniest month with 250 hours recorded sunshine; December the least with 58 hours recorded sunshine.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> 50% of the days are overcast.\n</p><p>A number of records were set in 2014. It was the highest annual mean temperature of 12.4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (54.3&#160;\xc2\xb0F). This is 0.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (0.54&#160;\xc2\xb0F) higher than for any other year, due to an almost complete absence of cold snaps during the winter months. Three very wet months meant that the winter was the wettest on record. Halloween turned out to be warmer than any other on record, with the temperature peaking at 18.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (64.9&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-GMO14_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMO14-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">9.0<br /> (48.2)\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align: center;">\n<th scope="row" style="height: 16px;">Record low \xc2\xb0C (\xc2\xb0F)\n</th>\n<td style="background: #BEBEFF;
