color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">1,864\n</td></tr>\n\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source &#35;1: Guernsey Met Office 2014 Weather Report<sup id="cite_ref-GMO14_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GMO14-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center; font-size:95%;">Source &#35;2: M\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9o Climat<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Guernsey" title="Geology of Guernsey">Geology of Guernsey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_landscape_2_(1993).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Guernsey_landscape_2_%281993%29.jpg/220px-Guernsey_landscape_2_%281993%29.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Guernsey_landscape_2_%281993%29.jpg/330px-Guernsey_landscape_2_%281993%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Guernsey_landscape_2_%281993%29.jpg/440px-Guernsey_landscape_2_%281993%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="666" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_landscape_2_(1993).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Guernsey coastal rocks</div></div></div>\n<p>Guernsey has a geological history stretching further back into the past than most of Europe. It forms part of the geological province of France known as the <a href="/wiki/Armorican_Massif" title="Armorican Massif">Armorican Massif</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> There is a broad geological division between the north and south of the Island. The Southern Metamorphic Complex is elevated above the geologically younger, lower lying Northern Igneous Complex. Guernsey has experienced a complex geological evolution (especially the rocks of the southern complex) with multiple phases of <a href="/wiki/Intrusive_rock" title="Intrusive rock">intrusion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fold_(geology)" title="Fold (geology)">deformation</a> recognisable.\n</p><p>Guernsey is composed of nine main rock types, two of which being <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granites</a> and the rest <a href="/wiki/Gneiss" title="Gneiss">gneiss</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Guernsey" title="Politics of Guernsey">Politics of Guernsey</a></div>\n<p>Guernsey is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> and legally a British <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependency" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown dependency">Crown dependency</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Guernsey" title="Lieutenant Governor of Guernsey">Lieutenant Governor of Guernsey</a> is the "representative of <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">the Crown</a> in right of the <i>r\xc3\xa9publique</i> of the Bailiwick of Guernsey".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Official_residence" title="Official residence">official residence</a> of the Lieutenant Governor is Government House. Since 2016 the incumbent has been <a href="/wiki/Vice_Admiral" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice Admiral">Vice Admiral</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/Ian_Corder" title="Ian Corder">Ian Corder</a> KBE, CB, replacing his predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Air_Marshal" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Marshal">Air Marshal</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Walker_(RAF_officer)" title="Peter Walker (RAF officer)">Peter Walker</a>, who had died in post.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The post was created in 1835 as a result of the abolition of the office of Governor. Since that point, the Lieutenant Governor has always resided locally.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="States_of_Guernsey">States of Guernsey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: States of Guernsey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/States_of_Guernsey" title="States of Guernsey">States of Guernsey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lieutenant_Governor_and_Bailiff_of_Guernsey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lieutenant_Governor_and_Bailiff_of_Guernsey.jpg/220px-Lieutenant_Governor_and_Bailiff_of_Guernsey.jpg" width="220" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lieutenant_Governor_and_Bailiff_of_Guernsey.jpg/330px-Lieutenant_Governor_and_Bailiff_of_Guernsey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lieutenant_Governor_and_Bailiff_of_Guernsey.jpg/440px-Lieutenant_Governor_and_Bailiff_of_Guernsey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1354" data-file-height="1226" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lieutenant_Governor_and_Bailiff_of_Guernsey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bailiff Richard Collas (right) attending the Queen\'s birthday parade 2016 in his formal robes</div></div></div>\n<p>The deliberative assembly of the States of Guernsey (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">\xc3\x89tats de Guernesey</i>) is called the States of Deliberation (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">\xc3\x89tats de D\xc3\xa9lib\xc3\xa9ration</i>) and consists of 38 People\'s Deputies, elected from multi- or single-member districts every four years. There are also two representatives from <a href="/wiki/Alderney" title="Alderney">Alderney</a>, a semi-autonomous dependency of the Bailiwick, but <a href="/wiki/Sark" title="Sark">Sark</a> sends no representative since it has its own legislature. The <a href="/wiki/Bailiff_of_Guernsey" title="Bailiff of Guernsey">Bailiff</a> or Deputy Bailiff preside in the assembly. There are also two non-voting members: H.M. Procureur (analogous to the role of <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Attorney General">Attorney General</a>) and H.M. Comptroller (analogous to <a href="/wiki/Solicitor_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Solicitor General">Solicitor General</a>), both appointed by the Crown and collectively known as the Law Officers of the Crown.\n</p><p>A <i>projet de loi</i> is the equivalent of a UK bill or a French <i>projet de loi</i>, and a law is the equivalent of a UK <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament_in_the_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of Parliament in the UK">act of parliament</a> or a French <i>loi</i>. A draft law passed by the States can have no legal effect until formally approved by Her Majesty in Council and promulgated by means of an <a href="/wiki/Order_in_council" class="mw-redirect" title="Order in council">order in council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Laws are given the Royal Sanction at regular meetings of the Privy Council in London, after which they are returned to the islands for formal registration at the <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_Guernsey#Royal_Court" title="Courts of Guernsey">Royal Court</a>. The States also make delegated legislation known as Ordinances (<i>Ordonnances</i>) and Orders (<i>ordres</i>) which do not require the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Assent" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Assent">Royal Assent</a>. Commencement orders are usually in the form of ordinances.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Policy_and_Resources_Committee_of_Guernsey" title="Policy and Resources Committee of Guernsey">Policy and Resources Committee</a> is responsible for Guernsey\'s constitutional and external affairs, developing strategic and corporate policy and coordinating States business. It also examines proposals and Reports placed before Guernsey\'s Parliament (the States of Deliberation) by Departments and Non States Bodies. The President of the Committee is the de facto head of government of Guernsey.<sup id="cite_ref-P&amp;R_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-P&amp;R-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Legal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Guernsey" title="Law of Guernsey">Law of Guernsey</a></div>\n<p>Guernsey\'s legal system originates in Norman Customary Law, overlaid with principles taken from <a href="/wiki/English_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="English common law">English common law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equity_(law)" title="Equity (law)">Equity</a> as well as from statute law enacted by the competent legislature(s) \xe2\x80\x93 usually, but not always,  the States of Guernsey. Guernsey has almost complete autonomy over internal affairs and certain external matters. However, the Crown \xe2\x80\x93 that is to say, the UK Government \xe2\x80\x93 retains an ill-defined reserved power to intervene in the domestic affairs of any of the five Crown Dependencies within the <a href="/wiki/British_Islands" title="British Islands">British Islands</a> "in the interests of good government".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The UK Parliament is also a source of Guernsey law for those matters which are reserved to the UK, namely defence and foreign affairs.\n</p><p>The head of the judiciary in Guernsey is the Bailiff, who, as well as performing the judicial functions of a Chief Justice, is also the head of the States of Guernsey and has certain civic, ceremonial and executive functions. The Bailiff\'s functions may be exercised by the Deputy Bailiff. The posts of Bailiff and Deputy Bailiff are Crown appointments. Sixteen Jurats, who need no specific legal training, are elected by the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Election" title="States of Election">States of Election</a> from among Islanders. They act as a jury, as judges in civil and criminal cases and fix the sentence in criminal cases. First mentioned in 1179, there is a list of Jurats who have served since 1299.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The oldest <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_Guernsey" title="Courts of Guernsey">Courts of Guernsey</a> can be traced back to the 9th century. The principal court is the Royal Court and exercises both civil and criminal jurisdiction. Additional courts, such as the Magistrate\'s Court, which deals with minor criminal matters, and the Court of Appeal, which hears appeals from the Royal Court, have been added to the Island\'s legal system over the years.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="External_relations">External relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: External relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/External_relations_of_Guernsey" title="External relations of Guernsey">External relations of Guernsey</a></div>\n<p>Several European countries have a consular presence within the jurisdiction. The French Consulate is based at <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugo" title="Victor Hugo">Victor Hugo</a>\'s former residence at <a href="/wiki/Hauteville_House" title="Hauteville House">Hauteville House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the jurisdiction of Guernsey has complete autonomy over internal affairs and certain external matters, the topic of complete independence from the British Crown has been discussed widely and frequently, with ideas ranging from Guernsey obtaining independence as a Dominion to the bailiwicks of Guernsey and Jersey uniting and forming an independent Federal State within the Commonwealth, whereby both islands retain their independence with regards to domestic affairs but internationally, the islands would be regarded as one state.<sup id="cite_ref-HoG_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoG-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parishes">Parishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Parishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_(zoom),_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Guernsey_%28zoom%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg/450px-Guernsey_%28zoom%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg.png" width="450" height="307" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Guernsey_%28zoom%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg/675px-Guernsey_%28zoom%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Guernsey_%28zoom%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg/900px-Guernsey_%28zoom%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="522" data-file-height="356" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_(zoom),_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The parishes of Guernsey.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Guernsey" title="Parishes of Guernsey">Parishes of Guernsey</a></div>\n<p>Guernsey has ten <a href="/wiki/Parish_(administrative_division)" title="Parish (administrative division)">parishes</a>, which act as civil administration districts, with limited powers. Each parish is administered by a Douzaine, usually made up of twelve members, known as Douzeniers. Douzeniers are elected for a six-year mandate, two Douzeniers being elected by parishioners at a parish meeting in November each year. The senior Douzenier is known as the Doyen (Dean). Two elected <a href="/wiki/Conn%C3%A9table_(Jersey_and_Guernsey)" title="Conn\xc3\xa9table (Jersey and Guernsey)">Constables</a> (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Conn\xc3\xa9tables</i>) carry out the decisions of the Douzaine, serving for between one and three years. The longest serving Constable is known as the Senior Constable and his or her colleague as the Junior Constable.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The Douzaines levy an Occupiers Rate on properties to provide funding for running of the administration.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Guernsey\'s <a href="/wiki/Parish_(Church_of_England)" title="Parish (Church of England)">Church of England parishes</a> fall under the <a href="/wiki/See_of_Canterbury" class="mw-redirect" title="See of Canterbury">See of Canterbury</a>, having split from the <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Winchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishopric of Winchester">Bishopric of Winchester</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The biggest parish is Castel, while the most populated is St Peter Port.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Financial services, such as banking, <a href="/wiki/Investment_management" title="Investment management">fund management</a>, and insurance, account for about 37% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-www.gov.gg_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.gov.gg-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Tourism, manufacturing, and horticulture, mainly tomatoes and cut flowers, especially <a href="/wiki/Freesia" title="Freesia">freesias</a>, have been declining.<sup id="cite_ref-Tomato_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tomato-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Light tax and death duties make Guernsey a popular <a href="/wiki/Offshore_finance" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore finance">offshore finance</a> centre for <a href="/wiki/Private_equity_fund" title="Private equity fund">private equity funds</a>.\n</p><p>Guernsey does not have a Central Bank and it issues its own <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">sterling</a> <a href="/wiki/Coins_of_the_Guernsey_pound" class="mw-redirect" title="Coins of the Guernsey pound">coinage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_pound#Banknotes" title="Guernsey pound">banknotes</a>. UK coinage and (English, Scottish and Northern Irish-faced) banknotes also circulate freely and interchangeably.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Total island investment funds, used to fund pensions and future island costs, amount to \xc2\xa32.7billion as at June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The island issued a 30-year bond in December 2015 for \xc2\xa3330m, its first bond in 80 years.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The island has been given a credit rating of AA-/A-1+ with a stable outlook from <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor&#39;s">Standard &amp; Poor\'s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Guernsey has the official <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-2" title="ISO 3166-1 alpha-2">ISO 3166-1 alpha-2</a> code <b>GG</b> and the official <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-3" title="ISO 3166-1 alpha-3">ISO 3166-1 alpha-3</a> code <b>GGY</b>; <a href="/wiki/Market_data" title="Market data">market data</a> vendors, such as <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a>, will report products related to Guernsey using the alpha-3 code.\n</p><p>In March 2016 there were over 32,291 people employed in Guernsey with 4,864 being self-employed. 2,453 employing businesses. 19.6% work in the finance industry and median earnings were \xc2\xa331,215.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_Postbox_type_C_double_aperture_pillar_box.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Guernsey_Postbox_type_C_double_aperture_pillar_box.jpg/220px-Guernsey_Postbox_type_C_double_aperture_pillar_box.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Guernsey_Postbox_type_C_double_aperture_pillar_box.jpg/330px-Guernsey_Postbox_type_C_double_aperture_pillar_box.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Guernsey_Postbox_type_C_double_aperture_pillar_box.jpg/440px-Guernsey_Postbox_type_C_double_aperture_pillar_box.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_Postbox_type_C_double_aperture_pillar_box.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Guernsey Post pillar box.</div></div></div>\n<p>Public services, such as water, wastewater, the two main harbours and the airport are still owned and controlled by the States of Guernsey. The electricity, and postal services have been commercialised by the States and are now operated by companies wholly owned by the States of Guernsey. Gas is supplied by an independent private company. In 1998, Guernsey and Jersey jointly formed the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands_Electricity_Grid" title="Channel Islands Electricity Grid">Channel Islands Electricity Grid</a> to operate and manage the submarine cables between Europe and the Channel Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The installation of these cables provided the island with a secure form of backup power, having previously only had access to diesel generators.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Telecoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Guernsey Telecoms">Guernsey Telecoms</a>, which provided telecommunications, was sold by the States to <a href="/wiki/Cable_%26_Wireless_plc" title="Cable &amp; Wireless plc">Cable &amp; Wireless plc</a>, rebranded as <a href="/wiki/Sure_(company)" title="Sure (company)">Sure</a> and was sold to <a href="/wiki/Batelco" title="Batelco">Batelco</a> in April 2013. Newtel was the first alternative telecommunications company on the island and was acquired by Wave Telecom in 2010<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and subsequently rebranded as <a href="/wiki/Jersey_Telecom" class="mw-redirect" title="Jersey Telecom">Jersey Telecom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Airtel-Vodafone" title="Airtel-Vodafone">Airtel-Vodafone</a> also provide a mobile network.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Both the <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Post" title="Guernsey Post">Guernsey Post</a> postal boxes (since 1969) and the telephone boxes (since 2002) are painted blue, but otherwise are identical to their British counterparts, the red <a href="/wiki/Pillar_box" title="Pillar box">pillar box</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_telephone_box" title="Red telephone box">red telephone box</a>. In 2009 the telephone boxes at the bus station were painted yellow just like they used to be when Guernsey Telecoms was state-owned. The oldest pillar box still in use in the British Isles can be found in Union Street, St Peter Port and dates back to 1853.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ATR_42-500_of_Aurigny_Air_Services_(G-HUET)_takes_off_from_Bristol_Airport,_England_8Sept2016_arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/ATR_42-500_of_Aurigny_Air_Services_%28G-HUET%29_takes_off_from_Bristol_Airport%2C_England_8Sept2016_arp.jpg/220px-ATR_42-500_of_Aurigny_Air_Services_%28G-HUET%29_takes_off_from_Bristol_Airport%2C_England_8Sept2016_arp.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/ATR_42-500_of_Aurigny_Air_Services_%28G-HUET%29_takes_off_from_Bristol_Airport%2C_England_8Sept2016_arp.jpg/330px-ATR_42-500_of_Aurigny_Air_Services_%28G-HUET%29_takes_off_from_Bristol_Airport%2C_England_8Sept2016_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/ATR_42-500_of_Aurigny_Air_Services_%28G-HUET%29_takes_off_from_Bristol_Airport%2C_England_8Sept2016_arp.jpg/440px-ATR_42-500_of_Aurigny_Air_Services_%28G-HUET%29_takes_off_from_Bristol_Airport%2C_England_8Sept2016_arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3494" data-file-height="2490" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ATR_42-500_of_Aurigny_Air_Services_(G-HUET)_takes_off_from_Bristol_Airport,_England_8Sept2016_arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/ATR_42-500" class="mw-redirect" title="ATR 42-500">ATR 42-500</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aurigny_Air_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Aurigny Air Services">Aurigny Air Services</a> takes off from <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Airport" title="Bristol Airport">Bristol Airport</a>, England (2016).</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Guernsey" title="Transport in Guernsey">Transport in Guernsey</a></div>\n<p>Ports and harbours exist at <a href="/wiki/St_Peter_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="St Peter Port">St Peter Port</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Sampson,_Guernsey" title="Saint Sampson, Guernsey">St Sampson</a>. There is a single paved airport, <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Airport" title="Guernsey Airport">Guernsey Airport</a>. The <a href="/wiki/States_of_Guernsey" title="States of Guernsey">States of Guernsey</a> wholly own their own airline, <a href="/wiki/Aurigny" title="Aurigny">Aurigny</a>. The decision to purchase the airline was made to protect important air links to and from the island and the sale was completed on 15 May 2003.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Railway" title="Guernsey Railway">Guernsey Railway</a>, effectively an electric <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramway</a>, began working on 20 February 1892 and was abandoned on 9 June 1934. It replaced an earlier transport system which was worked by steam, the Guernsey Steam Tramway, which had operated from 6 June 1879 with six locomotives. Alderney is now the only Channel Island with a <a href="/wiki/Alderney_Railway" title="Alderney Railway">working railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Guernsey has a public bus service, operated by CT Plus on behalf of the States of Guernsey Environment and Infrastructure Department.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the finance industry forms the largest economic sector in Guernsey, generating around 40% of Guernsey\'s GDP and directly employing around 21% of its workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Banks began setting up operations in the island from the early 1960s onwards in order to avoid high onshore taxes and restrictive regulation.<sup id="cite_ref-Crossan17_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crossan17-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The industry regulator is the <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Financial_Services_Commission" title="Guernsey Financial Services Commission">Guernsey Financial Services Commission</a>, which was established in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prior to the growth of the finance industry, the island\'s main industries were quarrying and horticulture. The latter particularly decline as a result of the oil price shocks of the 1970s and the introduction of cheap <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> gas that benefited Dutch growers.<sup id="cite_ref-Crossan17_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crossan17-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Guernsey is home to <a href="/wiki/Specsavers" title="Specsavers">Specsavers</a> Optical Group and <a href="/wiki/Healthspan" title="Healthspan">Healthspan</a> also has its headquarters in Guernsey.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_towers.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Guernsey_towers.JPG/220px-Guernsey_towers.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Guernsey_towers.JPG/330px-Guernsey_towers.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Guernsey_towers.JPG/440px-Guernsey_towers.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_towers.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Towers in Guernsey</div></div></div>\n<p>Guernsey has been a tourist destination since at least the Victorian days, with the first tourist guide published in 1834. In the 19th century, two rail companies (<a href="/wiki/London_and_South_Western_Railway" title="London and South Western Railway">London and South Western Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway" title="Great Western Railway">Great Western Railway</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>) ran competing boats from the UK mainland to St Peter Port, with a race to the only convenient berth. This was halted with the sinking of the <a href="/wiki/SS_Stella_(1890)" title="SS Stella (1890)">SS <i>Stella</i></a> in 1899.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Guernsey enters <a href="/wiki/Britain_in_Bloom" title="Britain in Bloom">Britain in Bloom</a> with <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin,_Guernsey" title="Saint Martin, Guernsey">St Martin</a> Parish winning the small town category twice in 2006 and 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_Port" title="Saint Peter Port">Saint Peter Port</a> winning the large coastal category in 2014 and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter,_Guernsey" title="Saint Peter, Guernsey">St Peter\'s</a> winning the small coastal prize in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Herm has won Britain in Bloom categories several times:<sup id="cite_ref-BIB_2_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BIB_2-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> in 2002, 2008, and 2012, Herm won the Britain in Bloom Gold Award.<sup id="cite_ref-BIB_Dates_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BIB_Dates-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The military history of the island has left a number of fortifications, including <a href="/wiki/Castle_Cornet" title="Castle Cornet">Castle Cornet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Grey" title="Fort Grey">Fort Grey</a>. <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_loophole_towers" title="Guernsey loophole towers">Guernsey loophole towers</a> and a large collection of <a href="/wiki/German_fortification_of_Guernsey" title="German fortification of Guernsey">German fortifications</a> with a number of museums.\n</p><p>The use of the roadstead in front of St Peter Port by over 100 cruise ships a year is bringing over 100,000 day trip passengers to the island each year.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Guernsey, Alderney and Sark each raise their own taxation,<sup id="cite_ref-MOJ_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOJ-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> although in 1949 Alderney (but not Sark) transferred its fiscal rights to Guernsey.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Personal tax liability differs according to whether an individual is resident in the island or not. Individuals resident in the Jurisdiction of Guernsey (which does not include Sark) pay <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> at the rate of 20% on their worldwide income, whereas non-residents are only liable on income arising from activity or ownership within Guernsey. Unlike in the UK, the income tax year in Guernsey aligns to the calendar year.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2008, Guernsey has operated three levels of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">corporation tax</a>, depending on the source of the income.\n</p>\n<ul><li>A 0% corporation tax rate on most companies.</li>\n<li>A 10% rate (income from banking business and, with effect from 1 January 2013, extended to domestic insurance business, fiduciary business, insurance intermediary business and insurance manager business).</li>\n<li>A 20% rate (income from trading activities regulated by the Office of the Director General of Utility Regulation, and income from the ownership of lands and buildings).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Guernsey levies no <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_tax" title="Inheritance tax">inheritance</a>, capital transfer, value added (VAT / TVA) or general withholding taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In the 2011 Budget, the UK announced that it would be ending Low Value Consignment Relief that was being used to sell goods VAT free to customers across the UK, with this legislation coming into force on 1 April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Tax revenues represent 22.4% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-gov.gg_tax_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov.gg_tax-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The population is 63,026 (July 2016 est.).<sup id="cite_ref-population_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-population-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The median age for males is 40 years and for females is 42 years. The population growth rate is 0.775% with 9.62 births/1,000 population, 8 deaths/1,000 population, and annual net migration of 6.07/1,000 population. The life expectancy is 80.1 years for males and 84.5 years for females.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The Bailiwick ranked 10th in the world in 2015 with an average life expectancy of 82.47 years.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_control">Border control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Border control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The whole jurisdiction of Guernsey is part of the <a href="/wiki/Common_Travel_Area" title="Common Travel Area">Common Travel Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For immigration and nationality purposes it is UK law, and not Guernsey law, which applies (technically the Immigration Act 1971,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> extended to Guernsey by Order-in-Council). Guernsey may not apply different immigration controls to the UK.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing_restrictions">Housing restrictions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Housing restrictions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Guernsey undertakes a population management mechanism using restrictions over who may work in the island through control of which properties people may live in. The housing market is split between <i>local market</i> properties and a set number of <i>open market</i> properties.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Anyone may live in an open market property, but local market properties can only be lived in by those who qualify \xe2\x80\x93 either through being born in Guernsey (to at least one local parent), by obtaining a housing licence, or by virtue of sharing a property with someone who does qualify (living <i>en famille</i>). Consequently, <i>open market</i> properties are much more expensive both to buy and to rent. Housing licences are for fixed periods, often only valid for 4 years and only as long as the individual remains employed by a specified Guernsey employer. The licence will specify the type of accommodation and be specific to the address the person lives in,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> and is often subject to a police record check. These restrictions apply equally regardless of whether the property is owned or rented, and only apply to occupation of the property. Thus a person whose housing licence expires may continue to own a Guernsey property, but will no longer be able to live in it. There are no restrictions on who may own a property.\n</p><p>There are a number of routes to qualifying as a "local" for housing purposes. Generally, it is sufficient to be born to at least one Guernsey parent and to live in the island for ten years in a twenty-year period. In a similar way a partner (married or otherwise) of a local can acquire local status. Multiple problems arise following early separation of couples, especially if they have young children or if a local partner dies, in these situations personal circumstances and compassion can add weight to requests for local status. Once "local" status has been achieved it remains in place for life. Even a lengthy period of residence outside Guernsey does not invalidate "local" housing status.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although Guernsey\'s inhabitants are full <a href="/wiki/British_nationality_law" title="British nationality law">British citizens</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> an endorsement restricting the right of establishment in other European Union states is placed in the passport of British citizens connected solely with the Channel Islands and <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>. If classified with "Islander Status", the British passport will be endorsed as follows: \'The holder is not entitled to benefit from EU provisions relating to employment or establishment\'. Those who have a parent or grandparent born in the United Kingdom itself (England, Scotland, Wales and Northern Ireland), or who have lived in the United Kingdom for 5 years, are not subject to this restriction.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Guernsey" title="List of schools in Guernsey">List of schools in Guernsey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_College_Guernsey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Elizabeth_College_Guernsey.jpg/220px-Elizabeth_College_Guernsey.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Elizabeth_College_Guernsey.jpg/330px-Elizabeth_College_Guernsey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Elizabeth_College_Guernsey.jpg/440px-Elizabeth_College_Guernsey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_College_Guernsey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_College,_Guernsey" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth College, Guernsey">Elizabeth College</a>, in St Peter Port, Guernsey</div></div></div>\n<p>Teaching in Guernsey is based on the English National Curriculum. There are 10 primary schools, plus two junior schools and three infant schools. As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the island still has the 11-plus exam and pupils then transfer to one of four 11\xe2\x80\x9316 secondary schools, or a co-educational grammar school.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> There are also three fee-paying colleges with lower schools, for which pupils over 11 receive grant support from the States of Guernsey. In 2016, the States of Guernsey voted to end the use of the 11-plus exams from 2019 onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> It is also responsible for education on the neighbouring islands.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Education Department is part way through a programme of re-building its secondary schools. The Department has completed the building of Le Rondin special needs school, the Sixth Form Centre at the Grammar School and the first phase of the new College of Further Education \xe2\x80\x93 a performing arts centre. The construction of St Sampsons High was completed summer 2008 and admitted its first pupils in September 2008.\n</p><p>In 2008, the school leaving age was raised so the earliest date is the last Friday in June in the year a pupil turns 16, in line with England, Wales and Northern Ireland. This means pupils will be between 15 and 10 months and 16 and 10 months before being able to leave. Prior to this, pupils could leave school at the end of the term in which they turned 14, if they so wished: a letter was required to be sent to the Education department to confirm this. However, this option was undertaken by relatively few pupils, the majority choosing to complete their GCSEs and then either begin employment or continue their education.\n</p><p>Post-<a href="/wiki/GCSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GCSE">GCSE</a> pupils have a choice of transferring to the state run <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Grammar_School_and_Sixth_Form_Centre" title="Guernsey Grammar School and Sixth Form Centre">Grammar School &amp; Sixth Form Centre</a>, or to the independent colleges for academic AS/A Levels/International Baccalureate Diploma Programme. They also have the option to study vocational subjects at the island\'s <i>Guernsey College of Further Education</i>.\n</p><p>There are no universities in the island. Students who attend university in the United Kingdom receive state support towards both maintenance and tuition fees. In 2007, the Education Department received the approval of the States Assembly to introduce student contributions to the costs of higher education, in the form of student loans, as apply in the UK. However, immediately after the general election of 2008, the States Assembly voted in favour of a <a href="/wiki/Private_member%27s_bill" title="Private member&#39;s bill">Requ\xc3\xaate</a> which proposed abolishing the student loans scheme on the grounds that it was expensive to run and would potentially discourage students from going to, and then returning to the island from, university. In 2012, the Education Department reported to the States Assembly that it had no need to re-examine the basis of higher education funding at the present time.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Guernsey" title="Culture of Guernsey">Culture of Guernsey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:George_M%C3%A9tivier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/George_M%C3%A9tivier.jpg/220px-George_M%C3%A9tivier.jpg" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/George_M%C3%A9tivier.jpg/330px-George_M%C3%A9tivier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/George_M%C3%A9tivier.jpg/440px-George_M%C3%A9tivier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="920" data-file-height="1046" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:George_M%C3%A9tivier.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/George_M%C3%A9tivier" title="George M\xc3\xa9tivier">George M\xc3\xa9tivier</a></div></div></div>\n<p>English is the language in general use by the majority of the population, while <a href="/wiki/Guern%C3%A9siais" title="Guern\xc3\xa9siais">Guern\xc3\xa9siais</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Norman_language" title="Norman language">Norman language</a> of the island, is spoken fluently by only about 2% of the population (according to 2001 census). However, 14% of the population claim some understanding of the language. Until the early 20th-century French was the only official language of the Bailiwick, and all deeds for the sale and purchase of real estate in Guernsey were written in French until 1971. Family and place names reflect this linguistic heritage. <a href="/wiki/George_M%C3%A9tivier" title="George M\xc3\xa9tivier">George M\xc3\xa9tivier</a>, a poet, wrote in Guernesiais. The loss of the island\'s language and the Anglicisation of its culture, which began in the 19th century and proceeded inexorably for a century, accelerated sharply when the majority of the island\'s school children were evacuated to the UK for five years during the German occupation of 1940\xe2\x80\x9345.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Renoir16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Renoir16.jpg/220px-Renoir16.jpg" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Renoir16.jpg/330px-Renoir16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Renoir16.jpg/440px-Renoir16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="704" data-file-height="589" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Renoir16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Children on the Beach of Guernsey</i> (1883) by Pierre-Auguste Renoir.</div></div></div>\n<p>The French <a href="/wiki/Impressionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Impressionist">impressionist</a> painter <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Auguste_Renoir" title="Pierre-Auguste Renoir">Pierre-Auguste Renoir</a> visited the island in late summer 1883. While on the island, he painted fifteen pictures of the views on the island, all featuring the bay and beach of Moulin Huet on the south coast.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_cow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Guernsey_cow.jpg/220px-Guernsey_cow.jpg" width="220" height="314" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Guernsey_cow.jpg/330px-Guernsey_cow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Guernsey_cow.jpg/440px-Guernsey_cow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2546" data-file-height="3633" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guernsey_cow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Guernsey cow</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_cattle" title="Guernsey cattle">Guernsey cow</a> is an internationally famous icon of the island. As well as being prized for its rich creamy milk, which is claimed to hold health benefits over milk from other breeds,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Guernsey cattle are increasingly being raised for their distinctively flavoured and rich yellowy-fatted beef, with butter made from the milk of Guernsey cows also has a distinctive yellow colour.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1960s the number of individual islanders raising these cattle for private supply has diminished significantly, Guernsey steers can still be occasionally seen grazing on L\'Ancresse common.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Guernsey also hosts a breed of goat known as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Guernsey" title="Golden Guernsey">Golden Guernsey</a>, distinguished by its golden-coloured coat. At the end of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, the Golden Guernsey had almost been rendered extinct due to <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_(biology)" title="Hybrid (biology)">interbreeding</a> on the island. The survival of this breed is largely credited to the work of a single woman, Miriam Milbourne, who successfully hid her herd from the Germans during the occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Although no longer considered to be <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a>, the breed remains on the watchlist of the <a href="/wiki/Rare_Breeds_Survival_Trust" title="Rare Breeds Survival Trust">Rare Breeds Survival Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> The traditional explanation for the donkey (<i>\xc3\xa2ne</i> in French and Guern\xc3\xa9siais) is the steepness of St Peter Port streets that necessitated beasts of burden for transport (in contrast to the flat terrain of the rival capital of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helier" title="Saint Helier">St Helier</a> in Jersey), although it is also used in reference to Guernsey inhabitants\' stubbornness. In turn, Guernseymen traditionally refer to Jerseymen as <i><a href="/wiki/Crapaud" title="Crapaud">crapauds</a></i> ("<a href="/wiki/Toad" title="Toad">toads</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The so-called <a href="/wiki/Nerine_sarniensis" title="Nerine sarniensis">Guernsey Lily</a>, <i>Nerine sarniensis</i>, is also used as a symbol of the island, although this species was introduced to the island from South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A local delicacy is the <a href="/wiki/Abalone" title="Abalone">ormer</a> (<i>Haliotis tuberculata</i>), a variety of abalone harvested under strict laws from beaches at <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">low spring tides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Traditional Guernsey recipes include a stew called <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Bean_Jar" title="Guernsey Bean Jar">Guernsey Bean Jar</a>, that is particularly served at the annual <a href="/wiki/Viaer_Marchi" title="Viaer Marchi">Viaer Marchi</a> festival.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Chief ingredients include haricot and butter beans, pork and shin beef. <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_G%C3%A2che" title="Guernsey G\xc3\xa2che">Guernsey G\xc3\xa2che</a> is a special bread made with raisins, sultanas and mixed peel.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugo" title="Victor Hugo">Victor Hugo</a>, having arrived on Halloween 1855,<sup id="cite_ref-Cooper19_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cooper19-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> wrote some of his best-known works while in exile in Guernsey, including <i><a href="/wiki/Les_Mis%C3%A9rables" title="Les Mis\xc3\xa9rables">Les Mis\xc3\xa9rables</a></i>. His home in St Peter Port, Hauteville House, is now a museum administered by the city of <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. In 1866, he published a novel set on Guernsey, <i>Travailleurs de la Mer</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Toilers_of_the_Sea" title="Toilers of the Sea">Toilers of the Sea</a></i>), which he dedicated to the island. Guernsey was his home for fifteen years.<sup id="cite_ref-Cooper19_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cooper19-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mabel_Collins" title="Mabel Collins">Mabel Collins</a> (1851\xe2\x80\x931927), a <a href="/wiki/Theosophist" class="mw-redirect" title="Theosophist">theosophist</a> and prolific author, was born in St Peter Port, Guernsey.\n</p><p>Guernseyman <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Basil_Edwards" title="Gerald Basil Edwards">G. B. Edwards</a> wrote a critically acclaimed novel, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Ebenezer_Le_Page" title="The Book of Ebenezer Le Page">The Book of Ebenezer Le Page</a></i> that was published in 1981, including insights into Guernsey life during the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In September 2008, a <a href="/wiki/Blue_plaque" title="Blue plaque">blue plaque</a> was affixed to the house on the Braye Road where Edwards was raised.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Watson_Fowler" title="Henry Watson Fowler">Henry Watson Fowler</a> moved to Guernsey in 1903. He and his brother <a href="/wiki/Francis_George_Fowler" title="Francis George Fowler">Francis George Fowler</a> composed <i><a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_English" title="The King&#39;s English">The King\'s English</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Concise_Oxford_Dictionary" class="mw-redirect" title="Concise Oxford Dictionary">Concise Oxford Dictionary</a> and much of <i><a href="/wiki/Modern_English_Usage" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern English Usage">Modern English Usage</a></i> on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Guernsey" title="Sport in Guernsey">Sport in Guernsey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jersey_Town_Criterium_2010_53.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jersey_Town_Criterium_2010_53.jpg/220px-Jersey_Town_Criterium_2010_53.jpg" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jersey_Town_Criterium_2010_53.jpg/330px-Jersey_Town_Criterium_2010_53.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jersey_Town_Criterium_2010_53.jpg/440px-Jersey_Town_Criterium_2010_53.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1629" data-file-height="1543" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jersey_Town_Criterium_2010_53.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Joshua Gosselin racing for the Guernsey Velo Club</div></div></div>\n<p>Guernsey participates in the biennial <a href="/wiki/Island_Games" title="Island Games">Island Games</a>, which it hosted in 1987 and 2003 at <a href="/wiki/Footes_Lane" title="Footes Lane">Footes Lane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Guernsey has also participated as a country in its own right in <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> since <a href="/wiki/1970_British_Commonwealth_Games" title="1970 British Commonwealth Games">1970</a>. Its first medals came in <a href="/wiki/1982_Commonwealth_Games" title="1982 Commonwealth Games">1982</a> with its first gold in <a href="/wiki/1990_Commonwealth_Games" title="1990 Commonwealth Games">1990</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In those sporting events where Guernsey does not have international representation, but the British <a href="/wiki/Home_Nations" title="Home Nations">Home Nations</a> are competing separately, highly skilled islanders may choose to compete for any of the Home Nations. There are, however, restrictions on subsequent transfers to represent other Home Nations. The football player <a href="/wiki/Matt_Le_Tissier" title="Matt Le Tissier">Matt Le Tissier</a>, for example, could have played for the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scottish</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Welsh</a> football teams, but opted to play for <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> instead. Football in Guernsey is run by the <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Football_Association" title="Guernsey Football Association">Guernsey Football Association</a>. The top tier of Guernsey football is the FNB <a href="/wiki/Priaulx_League" title="Priaulx League">Priaulx League</a> where there are seven teams (Belgrave Wanderers, Northerners, Sylvans, St Martin\'s, Rovers, <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_Rangers_F.A.C." title="Guernsey Rangers F.A.C.">Rangers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vale_Recreation_F.C." title="Vale Recreation F.C.">Vale Recreation</a>). The second tier is the <a href="/wiki/Jackson_League" title="Jackson League">Jackson League</a>. In the 2011\xe2\x80\x9312 season, <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_F.C." title="Guernsey F.C.">Guernsey F.C.</a> was formed and entered the <a href="/wiki/Combined_Counties_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Combined Counties League">Combined Counties League</a> Division 1, becoming the first Channel Island club ever to compete in the English leagues. Guernsey became division champions comfortably on 24 March 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> they won the Combined Counties Premier Challenge Cup on 4 May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Their second season saw them promoted again on the final day in front of 1,754 \'Green Lions\' fans, this time to Division One South of the Isthmian League,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> despite their fixtures being heavily affected not only by poor winter weather, but by their notable progression to the semi-finals of the FA Vase cup competition.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> They play in level 8 of the <a href="/wiki/English_football_pyramid" class="mw-redirect" title="English football pyramid">English football pyramid</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Corbet_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Corbet Field">Corbet Football Field</a>, donated by Jurat Wilfred Corbet <a href="/wiki/OBE" class="mw-redirect" title="OBE">OBE</a> in 1932, has fostered the sport greatly over the years. Recently, the island upgraded to a larger, better-quality stadium, in Footes Lane.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Guernsey has the second oldest tennis club in the world, at Kings<sup id="cite_ref-kingstory_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingstory-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> (founded in 1857<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>), with courts built in 1875. The island has produced a world class tennis player in <a href="/wiki/Heather_Watson" title="Heather Watson">Heather Watson</a> as well as professional squash players in <a href="/wiki/Martine_Le_Moignan" title="Martine Le Moignan">Martine Le Moignan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Opie" title="Lisa Opie">Lisa Opie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Simpson_(squash_player)" title="Chris Simpson (squash player)">Chris Simpson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kingstory_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingstory-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Guernsey was declared an affiliate member by the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a> (ICC) in 2005 and an associate member in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_cricket_team" title="Guernsey cricket team">Guernsey cricket team</a> plays in the <a href="/wiki/World_Cricket_League" title="World Cricket League">World Cricket League</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Cricket_Championship" title="European Cricket Championship">European Cricket Championship</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Sussex_Cricket_League" title="Sussex Cricket League">Sussex Cricket League</a>.\n</p><p>Various forms of <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">motorsport</a> take place on the island, including races on the sands on Vazon beach as well as a quarter-mile "sprint" along the Vazon coast road. Le Val des Terres, a steeply winding road rising south from St Peter Port to Fort George, is often the focus of both local and international <a href="/wiki/Hill-climb" class="mw-redirect" title="Hill-climb">hill-climb</a> races. In addition, the 2005, 2006 and 2007 World Touring Car Champion <a href="/wiki/Andy_Priaulx" title="Andy Priaulx">Andy Priaulx</a> is a Guernseyman.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Racecourse" class="mw-redirect" title="Racecourse">racecourse</a> on <a href="/wiki/L%27Ancresse" title="L&#39;Ancresse">L\'Ancresse</a> Common was re-established in 2004 after a gap of 13 years, with the first new race occurring on 2 May 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Races are held on most May day <a href="/wiki/Bank_holiday" title="Bank holiday">bank holidays</a>, with competitors from Guernsey as well as Jersey, France and the UK participating. <a href="/wiki/Sea_angling" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea angling">Sea angling</a> around Guernsey and the other islands in the Bailiwick from shore or boat is a popular pastime for both locals and visitors with the Bailiwick boasting multiple UK records.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guernsey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Guernsey" title="Outline of Guernsey">Outline of Guernsey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Index_of_Guernsey-related_articles" title="Index of Guernsey-related articles">Index of Guernsey-related articles</a></li>\n<li><a
